PMOGRAM NO\n\nDELTA IMP\n\n\' 2509\n\n7.\n\nH t VI Slur*\n\nSPACECRAFT GEOMETRY\nThe geometric structure of the IMP-H spacecraft, as shown on page 1322, is a 16-sided drum measuring 53.4\ninches across the flats and 62 inches in overall height. The spacecraft consists of an aluminum honeycomb\nshelf which is supported by eight struts and an 18-inch diameter thrust tube on the underside. The experiments and instrument modules are mounted on the topside of the shelf, and a solid propellant kick motor for\norbit circularization is centcrally located in the upper part of the structure. The instrumentation midsection is fully inclosed by metallic covers and side panels to satisfy stringent RF shielding and thermal\nrequirements, while two bands of solar panels above the midsection and one below it supply electrical power\nto experiments and electronic when in orbit. Four active and four passive turnstile-type RF antennas,\nequally spaced, extend radially from a spacer between the two upper solar panel bands. Two 10-foot experiment booms and two 5-foot ACS booms are folded alongside the structure during launch and transfer phases,\nand then deployed to their extended positions bv ground command after final orbit is achieved.\nSTABILIZATION\nORIENTATION SENSOR SYSTEM\n\nj\n\nThe optical aspect system, consisting of sun and earth sensors and associated electronics, provides spin\naxis orientation data, spin rate data, and onboard sun orientation pulses.\nATTITUDE CONTROL SYSTEM\nThe attitude control system is a cold gas monopropellant system using Feron 14. It will be actuated by\nground command to align the kick motor for a near circular orbit, orient spacecraft spin axis normal to the\necliptic plane, and adjust spin rate.\n..\nSPIN RATES\n(1) During third stage burning:\n(2) Prior to boom deployment:\n(3) During normal .operations:\n\n40 to 50 rpm\n20 rpm\n46 rpin, adjusted by ACS command.\n\ni? This transmitter will be used for main telemetry data during launch and may be used during the first perigee\nshadow or if the \\2-watt transmitter fails. If the DST is not available at launch, the Delta instrumentation package will provide analog data\nvia two IRIG subcarriers (Channels 8 and 10). The analog telemetry data would be FM/FM/PM modulated \xc2\xb1 1 radian.\n\n(2)\n\nThe primary spacecraft to earth link will be 137.920 MHz, 12 watts, phase modulated.\nThis transmitter will be used for 800 or 3200 bps, split-phase PCM, convolutional coding, 1/2 rate code (i.e., only 1/2 bit rate is information;\nother half is parity). In the event the convolutional encoder fails, a complementary code will be used consisting of 4 bits data followed\nsequentially by 4 bits of the same data inverted. This transmitter will be off at launch and will be turned on by ground command within\none hour after separation.\n\n(3)\n\nEarth to spacecraft, 148.080 MHz. The structure consists of an\naluminum honeycomb shelf supported by eight struts and an 18-inch diameter thrust tube on tha underside. Experiment modules ore mounted on thd\ntopside of the shelf. To sotisfy the stringent RF and thermal requirements, the ?Scperiment section is fully enclosed by metallic cover\' r.d side p^.iils.\nThree solar array rings are used to supply power to tiie experiments and electronics when in orbit. Appended to the exterior of the structure are two\nexpsrimsnt booms and two attitude control system booms. These booms fold alongside the spacecraft and deploy at a preselected time and sequc-r.cc.\nThe IV.P-J spacecraft includes four 150-foot experiment antennas which are deployed after orbit has been achieved. M AM\n\nDELTA IMP\nb.\n\nf*\n\n7 . i \xe2\x80\xa2 K V I *i I; t r* .\xe2\x80\xa2)<>.\n\n2509\n\ny.\n1 UST\nC^UE\n\ni r t: \xc2\xbb-i HO.\n\ni\n\nA,G\n\nIt is requested that the command transmitter be set up to deviate +62.5 kHz \xc2\xb15\'\'t- per tone without\ncompression. The combined deviation for two simultaneously transmitted tones is to be no greater\nthan 125 kHz and no less than 113 kHz\n\n2\n\nA\n\nSending of ARM Function during first stage powered flight:\nSeparation of the first and second stages, and ignition of the second stage engine, occur by\nsequence 1 of the second stage programmer. The second stage programmer is started when the first\nfirst stage staging relay ( 7 ) is energinized from the MECO bus.\nK 4\nIf ARM is sent, the first stage VECO and MECO relays, and the MECO bus, are energized, but the\ncircuit from the MECO bus to the staging relay is interrupted. The main and vernier engines shut\ndown, but the second stage programmer is not started, and therefore separation does not occur.\nHowever, Lhe ARM relay does not have a lock-in feature. Removing the ARM\ncommand re-establisho:;\nthe connection from the staging relay to the MECO bus. Shutdown of the main engine has closed tlit\nFIP switches connecting the MECO bus to the MECO enable bus. Energizing the MECO enable bus is a\nfirst stage timer function, and the timer continues to run. Thus, removing ARM will result in\nblast band jettison and second stage programmer start, either immediately or when the MECO enable\nfunction time is reached.\nIn the second stage the ARM command actuates two relays. One relay provides a backup ARM signal\nfor first stage shutdown. Both relays establish connections from the engine start bus to the\nSECO bus. If there is no power on the engine start bus, establishing these connections causes no\nchange of state on the SECO bus. As there is no power on the engine start bus until second stage\nprogrammer Sequence 1 has occurred, and the ARM relays do not lock in, sending arid rt:nioving ARM\nbefore Sequence 1 will not preclude subsequent second stage ignition.\nSee the Flight Termination Report for further details.\n\nFOR:.: r<\nJULY 70\n\nI.\n\nCLASSIFICATION\n\nCLASSIFICATION\n\'\n\n\' """ \xe2\x80\x94 \xe2\x80\xa2 \xe2\x80\xa2 \' - "\n\n"\n\n*\xe2\x80\xa2\xe2\x80\xa2 "\n\n.,t.tl\xc2\xabni . . . l . . . . . ... \xc2\xbb..fc-f-\xc2\xab-i\xc2\xab.^..\xc2\xbb\nr l i. . ^ ; . !\n\n\xe2\x80\xa2!\xe2\x80\xa2\xe2\x80\xa2.. i~\xc2\xbb1l"n-.\xc2\xab.\n\n"l. PHOGRAM NO.\n\nfJO.\n\n2509\n\nIn order to assist in the determination of success or failure of a mission, and to assist in prediction of prelim\nminary orbital parameter\'s, the verfication and time of occurrence of Stage 3 spinup and separation are desired\nWhenever the launch look angles indicate that the event will occur after passage of the launch vehicle over the\nStation 1 radio horizon^ Or that the data from station 1 will be marginal due to low aspect angle or low signal\nstrength, the data should be received at a downrange site, normally Station 91.\nThis data should be recorded at the site on magnetic tape and on a direct write recorder for immediate readout by\nRange Contractor personnel. In addition, this data and selected PDM channels should be retransmitted in real ti\'im\nvia the SSB link, or subcable, to Station 1 (Hgr AE) for display and readout by project personnel at that site.\nFour items of information are desired: Occurrence of the events; time of spinup indication; time of separation\nindication; and general quality of the data at these times.\nThese times of spinup and separation should be reported as accurately as possible, but at least to within 1/2\nseconds (preferably 0.1 sec) in Zulu time. Any real-time recordings run for this purpose should not be stopped\nbut should continue to run to preclude any possibility of stopping on an erroneous indication and missing the real\nevents. A copy of these recordings should be supplied to the project.\nFor additional information, the times of spinup command and separation command (as opposed to the actual function\npreviously mentioned) should be recorded for backup.\nFor real-time retransmission of Stage 2 PDM on VCO E, it should not deviate more than \xc2\xb110% on the wide band subcable.\nTelemetry assignments and Wave Forms will be supplied when available.\n\nFOR" R 0/C\nJHI.Y70\nI.\n\nCLASSIFICATION\n\njj\n\n\\\n\n.\n\n-t\n\n\'\n\nZ\n\n"\n\n111.1}\n\n- W E ^ L A C e S PAGE\n\n(S)\n\nS. DESCRIPTION OF POSITIONING\n\nMETHODS AND E.OUIP.V1ENT\n\nThe vehicle is oriented on the launcher for a 115\xc2\xb0 azi:r.ut\nRetractable fuel and LOX masts ere mounted en the launch;\nThe service tower, in the retired position and using the\nmain hoist, raises the first and second stages off the\ntransporters and lowers the stages to the launcher. The\nsame procedure is followed using three alternate tower\nhoists in installing the solid engines. The third stage-.\nand S/C are erected by an alternate hoist with the tower\naround the vehicle.\n\n21. DESCRIPTION OF LAUNCHER\n\nThe launcher is a\npermanent type launcher with a fixed umbilical tower.\nThe tower surrounds the vehicle during prelaunch testing and is movable and\nself-propelled. The vehicle is supported on six legs, five permanent and one\nretractable. The legs contain screws to hold down the vehicle prior to launch.\nThe deck plating surrounding the legs is retracted for launch to expose the\ndeflector plate, directing exhaust eastward.\nFORM R S13\nJULY 70\nI.\n\nCLASSIFICATION\n\n*Based on RCA Systems Analysis Monthly Accuracy Bulletin\n17 dated 28 February 1966.\n\nI.\n\nCl-ASSIKlCATIC\'N\n\ns I.\n\n(PAGE T I T L E )\n\nR E P L A C E S PAGE (\xe2\x80\xa2)\n\nOTHER SUPPORT\n\nJ.
